Ever used the "Sign in with Google" or "Login with Facebook" button? That's OAuth in action! #OAuth (Open Authorization) is a security framework that allows apps to access your information without needing your password. Think of it like giving a friend a spare key to just your living room, not your whole house. Here's how it works in three easy steps: You Approve Access: When an app (like a fitness app) asks to access your Google account, OAuth steps in. You're redirected to Google to log in, but you never give the app your Google password. Google Issues a Key (Token): After you approve, Google gives a unique "access token" to the app. This token lets the app access ONLY the data you allowed, like your calendar or contacts. Limited Access, Full Security: Now, the app can fetch data (like your schedule) without storing your credentials. #Why Use OAuth? Keeps your password private Limits access to only what you approve Provides temporary access, revokable anytime #OAuth is the technology behind seamless logins, secure data sharing, and safe access in the apps we use every day. Next time you log in with Google or Facebook, you can thank OAuth for keeping things both simple and secure! ===POST_382=== DATE:2024-11-10 #Day91 AI + SQL: Instantly Turn Plain Text into Powerful Data Insights Today, data insights shouldn't require deep SQL knowledge. OpenTelemetry is an open-source observability framework that provides end-to-end visibility into applications by collecting metrics, logs, and traces. As a CNCF project, it unifies observability data, making it easier for developers to monitor and troubleshoot complex architectures. Why Use OpenTelemetry? • Unified Observability: OpenTelemetry combines metrics, traces, and logs into a single standard, eliminating the need for multiple observability tools. • Cross-Platform and Vendor-Neutral: It's compatible with major programming languages, cloud providers, and observability platforms, offering flexibility and reducing vendor lock-in. • Improved Performance and Troubleshooting: By correlating data from all parts of an application, OpenTelemetry speeds up root cause analysis, boosting performance and reliability. • Community-Driven and Open Source: Evolving based on community input, OpenTelemetry remains relevant to industry needs. How Does OpenTelemetry Work? 1. Data Collection: OpenTelemetry SDKs and agents are embedded in applications to gather observability data across programming languages and frameworks. 2. Instrumentation: It offers both automatic and manual instrumentation, allowing data collection at multiple levels to meet specific observability needs. 3. Data Exporting: Collected data is exported to preferred backends (like Prometheus, Grafana, or DataDog), encompassing metrics (performance), traces (request paths), and logs ===POST_391=== DATE:2024-11-02 #Day83 What is Splunk? However, in 2023, HashiCorp changed its license to a Business Source License (𝗕𝗦𝗟), limiting some usage rights. 𝗢𝗽𝗲𝗻𝗧𝗼𝗳𝘂: OpenTofu (formerly OpenTF) was created in response to Terraform's licensing change. It's a community-driven, open-source alternative, maintaining full open-source freedom. 𝗕𝗲𝗻𝗲𝗳𝗶𝘁𝘀 & 𝗨𝘀𝗲 𝗖𝗮𝘀𝗲𝘀 𝗧𝗲𝗿𝗿𝗮𝗳𝗼𝗿𝗺: Known for its established ecosystem and commercial support options, Terraform integrates seamlessly with cloud providers and HashiCorp tools like Vault and Consul. 𝗢𝗽𝗲𝗻𝗧𝗼𝗳𝘂: For companies valuing open-source freedom, OpenTofu offers the same IaC capabilities without the usage restrictions of BSL. It's ideal for avoiding lock-in and for teams that want control over their infrastructure roadmap. 𝗖𝗼𝘀𝘁-𝗕𝗲𝗻𝗲𝗳𝗶𝘁 𝗔𝗻𝗮𝗹𝘆𝘀𝗶𝘀 𝗧𝗲𝗿𝗿𝗮𝗳𝗼𝗿𝗺: Offers a free version, but larger companies may opt for Terraform Enterprise for advanced compliance and security, which comes at a cost. However, it's well-suited for enterprises needing support. 𝗢𝗽𝗲𝗻𝗧𝗼𝗳𝘂: As a free, open-source tool, OpenTofu eliminates licensing fees. However, it relies on community support, which can be a cost-saving but requires self-reliance for complex issues. Here are a few types to consider in this space: 1. #PGP/GPG (Pretty Good Privacy/GNU Privacy Guard) • #Type: Traditional Public Key Infrastructure (PKI) • #Description: PGP uses a public and private key pair for encryption and digital signatures. It's been widely used for email encryption, file encryption, and software signing since the 1990s. • #Usage: Best for those needing strong encryption and secure data exchanges, commonly used in email encryption, file protection, and data integrity. • #KeyManagement: Users generate and manage their own keys, which can be complex and requires good security practices. 2. #X.509 Certificates • #Type: Certificate-Based Public Key Infrastructure • #Description: X.509 is a standard that defines the format of public key certificates. X.509 certificates are used in SSL/TLS to authenticate websites, enabling secure communications over the internet. • #Usage: Commonly used for SSL/TLS certificates in HTTPS, VPN authentication, and digital document signing. • #KeyManagement: Managed by Certificate Authorities (CAs) like Let's Encrypt, DigiCert, etc., who verify identities before issuing certificates. This ensures trust in the certificates but involves a centralized trust authority. 3. #Sigstore • #Type: Keyless ===POST_396=== DATE:2024-10-28 #DAY79 #KubernetesMastery: The Updated Comprehensive Resource Welcome to the Updated Edition of Kubernetes Mastery: A Comprehensive Resource! Managing Layer #Caching Effectively • #Issue: Inefficient #caching can lead to unnecessary rebuilds, slowing down the process. • #Solution: Reorder Dockerfile commands by placing static dependencies before frequently changed layers (e.g., COPY commands). This optimizes Docker's #caching, meaning only final layers need rebuilding, reducing overall build time. 3. Ensuring Consistent #Dependencies Across Stages • #Issue: Inconsistent library versions across stages can cause runtime errors. • #Solution: Use the same base image across stages to maintain consistency, and specify exact dependency versions in package managers. #DependencyManagement provides stability and predictability across build stages. 4. #Debugging Intermediate Stages Efficiently • #Issue: Errors in multi-stage builds can be hard to trace, especially in intermediate stages. • #Solution: Use Docker's --target flag to stop the build at specific stages and debug incrementally. Various #testing tools are used to detect issues early. Static Code Analysis Tools like #SonarQube, #CodeQL, and #Veracode scan code to catch bugs and security issues before they reach production. This "shift-left" approach to security saves time and cost by identifying problems early. Dynamic Application Security Testing (DAST) #DAST tools (e.g., #OWASP ZAP, #Burp Suite) simulate attacks on a running application to detect runtime vulnerabilities like #SQL injection and #XSS. Integrating DAST in #CI/CD pipelines ensures continuous security. Software Composition Analysis (SCA) SCA tools (like #Snyk and #WhiteSource) scan your software for #open-source components and their vulnerabilities, ensuring compliance and reducing risks from third-party dependencies. Infrastructure as Code (IaC) Scanning #IaC scanning tools (#Checkov, #AWS Config) review code for infrastructure setups (e.g., Terraform files) to enforce #security policies and prevent misconfigurations, maintaining compliance standards. Container Security Scanning Tools like #Trivy and #Anchore scan #container images (e.g., Docker) to find vulnerabilities before deployment. With the rise of containerization, organizations are faced with a critical choice between deploying monolithic applications or adopting a microservices architecture. Let's explore how these two models interact with container technology and how they suit different business needs. Monolithic Applications A monolithic architecture is a traditional software design where all components of an application are combined into a single, unified unit. Historically, these applications were deployed as a single artifact on servers or VMs. #Monolithic in Containers #Simplicity: Monoliths are easy to containerize as everything is packaged into a single container. #Scaling Limitations: With monoliths, scaling means increasing the entire application, even if only one component needs more resources, leading to inefficiencies. #UseCase: Monolithic applications are ideal for smaller teams or legacy systems that don't require frequent updates or significant scalability. Microservices A #microservices architecture breaks down an application into smaller, independent services. Each service runs in its own container and communicates with other services via APIs. Microservices in Containers #Efficiency: Microservices can be independently containerized, allowing teams to scale, deploy, and manage each service separately. Resilience: If one microservice fails, the rest of the system remains operational, improvi ===POST_404=== DATE:2024-10-22 #Day72 Cost Optimization for Containers: Practical Case Studies with Compliance and Governance Reference Links: Kubernetes Cluster Autoscaler on GitHub: https://lnkd.in/guRiysUJ AWS Spot Instances Documentation : https://lnkd.in/gbUHEXDE Docker Multi-Stage Builds Documentation: Distroless Images on GitHub: https://lnkd.in/gEVrHwkf Google Cloud Run Documentation Google Preemptible VMs Azure Blob Storage Documentation : https://lnkd.in/g6kwVF8z Azure Kubernetes Service (AKS) Autoscaler : https://lnkd.in/guRiysUJ ===POST_405=== DATE:2024-10-21 Goodbye CentOS, Hello Rocky Linux, AlmaLinux, or RHEL! Coding Errors: Mistakes in code, like buffer overflows or incorrect input validation, can create exploitable vulnerabilities. 2. Outdated Software: Unpatched systems leave doors open for known exploits to enter. 3. Misconfigurations: Weak security setups, like default settings or poorly configured access controls, can be easily compromised. 4. Dependency Risks: Many systems use third-party libraries. Outdated or insecure libraries introduce vulnerabilities into otherwise secure environments. 5. Weak Authentication: Insecure password policies or lack of multi-factor authentication can expose systems to attackers. #How to #ReduceCVEs: 1. Use #MinimalBaseImages: Distroless images, for example, strip away unnecessary components, reducing the attack surface significantly. Chainguard 2. Continuous #VulnerabilityScanning: Automated tools like Snyk TRIVY and Aqua Security can help you stay on top of vulnerabilities by scanning code and infrastructure in real-time. 3. #Patch and Update Regularly: Implement a proactive patch management system to ensure that no vulnerabilities remain unaddressed. 4. #SBOM (Software Bill of Materials): Tools like Chainguard SBOM offer full transparency into every component of your software stack, making it easier to identify and patch at-risk dependencies. 5. #DevSecOps Practices: Embed security checks early into your CI/CD pipeline. Here's what I learned: → They store videos in an object store and use CDN for low-latency → They run infrastructure across many regions for low latency and high availability → They stream video timestamp data and store it in a key-value database for bookmarks → They store movie catalogs in a document data store for flexible data schema support → They use the cache-aside pattern to reduce the load on the document data store for movie catalog → They use machine learning to recommend movies and store results in a key-value store → They store the movie watchlist in a key-value database for simplicity → They pre-partition the DynamoDB tables to prevent throttling on scale → They route read traffic randomly to avoid the hot shard problem ⬳ 👋 PS - I wrote an article with visuals of this case study in my newsletter: ➟ https://lnkd.in/eBnkwfY2 ⬳ If you liked this post: 🔔 Follow Neo Kim ♻ Repost to help others find it 💾 Save this post for future reference ===POST_437=== DATE:2024-09-17 #Day37 Unlock Efficient #DevOps with #Visual Studio Code (VS Code) What is #VSCode?
